If enabled, each Django-powered page will be cached based on\nURL. The canonical way to enable cache middleware is to set\n``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` as your first piece of middleware, and\n``FetchFromCacheMiddleware`` as the last::\n\n    MIDDLEWARE = [\n        'django.middleware.cache.UpdateCacheMiddleware',\n        ...\n        'django.middleware.cache.FetchFromCacheMiddleware'\n    ]\n\nThis is counterintuitive, but correct: ``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` needs to run\nlast during the response phase, which processes middleware bottom-up;\n``FetchFromCacheMiddleware`` needs to run last during the request phase, which\nprocesses middleware top-down.\n\nThe single-class ``CacheMiddleware`` can be used for some simple sites.\nHowever, if any other piece of middleware needs to affect the cache key, you'll\nneed to use the two-part ``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` and\n``FetchFromCacheMiddleware``. This'll most often happen when you're using\nDjango's ``LocaleMiddleware``.\n\nMore details about how the caching works:\n\n* Only GET or HEAD-requests with status code 200 are cached.\n\n* The number of seconds each page is stored for is set by the \"max-age\" section\n  of the response's \"Cache-Control\" header, falling back to the\n  CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS setting if the section was not found.\n\n* This middleware expects that a HEAD request is answered with the same\n  response headers exactly like the corresponding GET request.\n\n* When a hit occurs, a shallow copy of the original response object is returned\n  from process_request.\n\n* Pages will be cached based on the contents of the request headers listed in\n  the response's \"Vary\" header.\n\n* This middleware also sets ETag, Last-Modified, Expires and Cache-Control\n  headers on the response object.\n\n\"\"\"\n\nimport time\n\nfrom django.conf import settings\nfrom django.core.cache import DEFAULT_CACHE_ALIAS, MiddlewareMixin\nfrom django.utils.http import parse_http_date_safe\n\n\nclass UpdateCacheMiddleware(MiddlewareMixin):\n    \"\"\"\n    Response-phase cache middleware that updates the cache if the response is\n    cacheable.\n\n    Must be used as part of the two-part update/fetch cache middleware.\n    UpdateCacheMiddleware must be the first piece of middleware in MIDDLEWARE\n    so that it'll get called last during the response phase.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(self, get_response):\n        super().__init__(get_response)\n        self.cache_timeout = settings.CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS\n        self.page_timeout = None\n        self.key_prefix = settings.CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX\n        self.cache_alias = settings.CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS\n\n    @property\n    def cache(self):\n        return caches[self.cache_alias]\n\n    def _should_update_cache(self, request, response):\n        return hasattr(request, \"_cache_update_cache\") and request._cache_update_cache\n\n    def process_response(self, request, response):\n        \"\"\"Set the cache, if needed.\"\"\"\n        if not self._should_update_cache(request, response):\n            # We don't need to update the cache, just return.\n            return response\n\n        if response.streaming or response.status_code not in (200, 304):\n            return response\n\n        # Don't cache responses that set a user-specific (and maybe security\n        # sensitive) cookie in response to a cookie-less request.\n        if (\n            not request.COOKIES\n            and response.cookies\n            and has_vary_header(response, \"Cookie\")\n        ):\n            return response\n\n        # Don't cache responses when the Cache-Control header is set to\n        # private, no-cache, or no-store.\n        cache_control = response.get(\"Cache-Control\", ())\n        if any(\n            directive in cache_control\n            for directive in (\n                \"private\",\n                \"no-cache\",\n                \"no-store\",\n            )\n        ):\n            return response\n\n        # Page timeout takes precedence over the \"max-age\" and the default\n        # cache timeout.\n        timeout = self.page_timeout\n        if timeout is None:\n            # The timeout from the \"max-age\" section of the \"Cache-Control\"\n            # header takes precedence over the default cache timeout.\n            timeout = get_max_age(response)\n            if timeout is None:\n                timeout = self.cache_timeout\n            elif timeout == 0:\n                # max-age was set to 0, don't cache.\n                return response\n        patch_response_headers(response, timeout)\n        if timeout and response.status_code == 200:\n            cache_key = learn_cache_key(\n                request, response, timeout, self.key_prefix, cache=self.cache\n            )\n            if hasattr(response, \"render\") and callable(response.render):\n                response.add_post_render_callback(\n                    lambda r: self.cache.set(cache_key, r, timeout)\n                )\n            else:\n                self.cache.set(cache_key, response, timeout)\n        return response\n\n\nclass FetchFromCacheMiddleware(MiddlewareMixin):\n    \"\"\"\n    Request-phase cache middleware that fetches a page from the cache.\n\n    Must be used as part of the two-part update/fetch cache middleware.\n    FetchFromCacheMiddleware must be the last piece of middleware in MIDDLEWARE\n    so that it'll get called last during the request phase.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(self, get_response):\n        super().__init__(get_response)\n        self.key_prefix = settings.CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX\n        self.cache_alias = settings.CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS\n\n    @property\n    def cache(self):\n        return caches[self.cache_alias]\n\n    def process_request(self, request):\n        \"\"\"\n        Check whether the page is already cached and return the cached\n        version if available.\n        \"\"\"\n        if request.method not in (\"GET\", \"HEAD\"):\n            request._cache_update_cache = False\n            return None  # Don't bother checking the cache.\n\n        # try and get the cached GET response\n        cache_key = get_cache_key(request, self.key_prefix, \"GET\", cache=self.cache)\n        if cache_key is None:\n            request._cache_update_cache = True\n            return None  # No cache information available, need to rebuild.\n        response = self.cache.get(cache_key)\n        # if it wasn't found and we are looking for a HEAD, try looking just\n        # for that\n        if response is None and request.method == \"HEAD\":\n            cache_key = get_cache_key(\n                request, self.key_prefix, \"HEAD\", cache=self.cache\n            )\n            response = self.cache.get(cache_key)\n\n        if response is None:\n            request._cache_update_cache = True\n            return None  # No cache information available, need to rebuild.\n\n        # Derive the age estimation of the cached response.\n        if (max_age_seconds := get_max_age(response)) is not None and (\n            expires_timestamp := parse_http_date_safe(response[\"Expires\"])\n        ) is not None:\n            now_timestamp = int(time.time())\n            remaining_seconds = expires_timestamp - now_timestamp\n            # Use Age: 0 if local clock got turned back.\n            response[\"Age\"] = max(0, max_age_seconds - remaining_seconds)\n\n        # hit, return cached response\n        request._cache_update_cache = False\n        return response\n\n\nclass CacheMiddleware(UpdateCacheMiddleware, FetchFromCacheMiddleware):\n    \"\"\"\n    Cache middleware that provides basic behavior for many simple sites.\n\n    Also used as the hook point for the cache decorator, which is generated\n    using the decorator-from-middleware utility.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(self, get_response, cache_timeout=None, page_timeout=None, **kwargs):\n        super().__init__(get_response)\n        # We need to differentiate between \"provided, but using default value\",\n        # and \"not provided\". If the value is provided using a default, then\n        # we fall back to system defaults. If it is not provided at all,\n        # we need to use middleware defaults.\n\n        try:\n            key_prefix = kwargs[\"key_prefix\"]\n            if key_prefix is None:\n                key_prefix = \"\"\n            self.key_prefix = key_prefix\n        except KeyError:\n            pass\n        try:\n            cache_alias = kwargs[\"cache_alias\"]\n            if cache_alias is None:\n                cache_alias = DEFAULT_CACHE_ALIAS\n            self.cache_alias = cache_alias\n        except KeyError:\n            pass\n\n        if cache_timeout is not None:\n            self.cache_timeout = cache_timeout\n        self.page_timeout = page_timeout\n","numLines":234,"startLine":1,"totalLines":234}}}

If enabled, each Django-powered page will be cached based on\nURL. The canonical way to enable cache middleware is to set\n``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` as your first piece of middleware, and\n``FetchFromCacheMiddleware`` as the last::\n\n    MIDDLEWARE = [\n        'django.middleware.cache.UpdateCacheMiddleware',\n        ...\n        'django.middleware.cache.FetchFromCacheMiddleware'\n    ]\n\nThis is counterintuitive, but correct: ``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` needs to run\nlast during the response phase, which processes middleware bottom-up;\n``FetchFromCacheMiddleware`` needs to run last during the request phase, which\nprocesses middleware top-down.\n\nThe single-class ``CacheMiddleware`` can be used for some simple sites.\nHowever, if any other piece of middleware needs to affect the cache key, you'll\nneed to use the two-part ``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` and\n``FetchFromCacheMiddleware``. This'll most often happen when you're using\nDjango's ``LocaleMiddleware``.\n\nMore details about how the caching works:\n\n* Only GET or HEAD-requests with status code 200 are cached.\n\n* The number of seconds each page is stored for is set by the \"max-age\" section\n  of the response's \"Cache-Control\" header, falling back to the\n  CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS setting if the section was not found.\n\n* This middleware expects that a HEAD request is answered with the same\n  response headers exactly like the corresponding GET request.\n\n* When a hit occurs, a shallow copy of the original response object is returned\n  from process_request.\n\n* Pages will be cached based on the contents of the request headers listed in\n  the response's \"Vary\" header.\n\n* This middleware also sets ETag, Last-Modified, Expires and Cache-Control\n  headers on the response object.\n\n\"\"\"","new_string":"\"\"\"\nFull-page cache middleware for Django.\n\nThis module provides cache middleware that caches entire HTTP responses based on\nthe request URL and method. When enabled, each Django-powered page will be\ncached and served from the cache on subsequent requests.\n\nConfiguration\n=============\n\nThere are two ways to enable caching:\n\n**Two-Part Middleware (Recommended)**\n    Use ``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` and ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware`` in your\n    middleware stack. This approach allows other middleware to influence the\n    cache key (e.g., ``LocaleMiddleware`` for locale-aware caching).\n\n    .. code-block:: python\n\n        MIDDLEWARE = [\n            'django.middleware.cache.UpdateCacheMiddleware',\n            # ... other middleware ...\n            'django.middleware.cache.FetchFromCacheMiddleware'\n        ]\n\n    Important: ``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` must be listed first (runs last during\n    response phase), and ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware`` must be listed last (runs\n    last during request phase).\n\n**Single-Class Middleware**\n    For simple sites, use ``CacheMiddleware`` instead:\n\n    .. code-block:: python\n\n        MIDDLEWARE = [\n            'django.middleware.cache.CacheMiddleware',\n            # ... other middleware ...\n        ]\n\nCaching Behavior\n================\n\n* Only GET and HEAD requests with HTTP status code 200 are cached.\n\n* Cache timeout is determined by (in order of precedence):\n    1. ``page_timeout`` parameter (if using CacheMiddleware)\n    2. ``max-age`` directive in the response's ``Cache-Control`` header\n    3. ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS`` Django setting\n\n* Responses with ``Cache-Control: private``, ``no-cache``, or ``no-store``\n  directives are never cached.\n\n* Cached pages are keyed by request URL and vary by headers listed in the\n  response's ``Vary`` header (e.g., ``Vary: Accept-Language, Cookie``).\n\n* Responses that set user-specific cookies (detected via ``Vary: Cookie`` header)\n  on cache-less requests are not cached for security.\n\n* HEAD requests are served from GET cache entries when available. If no GET\n  cache entry exists, a separate HEAD cache entry may be used.\n\n* When a cache hit occurs, a shallow copy of the cached response is returned,\n  with updated ``Age`` header reflecting response age.\n\n* Response headers are automatically patched with ``ETag``, ``Last-Modified``,\n  ``Expires``, and ``Cache-Control`` headers.\n\nSettings\n========\n\n* ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS``: Default cache timeout in seconds. Default: 600.\n* ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX``: Prefix for all cache keys. Default: ''.\n* ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS``: Cache alias to use. When enabled, each Django-powered page will be\ncached and served from the cache on subsequent requests.\n\nConfiguration\n=============\n\nThere are two ways to enable caching:\n\n**Two-Part Middleware (Recommended)**\n    Use ``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` and ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware`` in your\n    middleware stack. This approach allows other middleware to influence the\n    cache key (e.g., ``LocaleMiddleware`` for locale-aware caching).\n\n    .. code-block:: python\n\n        MIDDLEWARE = [\n            'django.middleware.cache.UpdateCacheMiddleware',\n            # ... other middleware ...\n            'django.middleware.cache.FetchFromCacheMiddleware'\n        ]\n\n    Important: ``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` must be listed first (runs last during\n    response phase), and ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware`` must be listed last (runs\n    last during request phase).\n\n**Single-Class Middleware**\n    For simple sites, use ``CacheMiddleware`` instead:\n\n    .. code-block:: python\n\n        MIDDLEWARE = [\n            'django.middleware.cache.CacheMiddleware',\n            # ... other middleware ...\n        ]\n\nCaching Behavior\n================\n\n* Only GET and HEAD requests with HTTP status code 200 are cached.\n\n* Cache timeout is determined by (in order of precedence):\n    1. ``page_timeout`` parameter (if using CacheMiddleware)\n    2. ``max-age`` directive in the response's ``Cache-Control`` header\n    3. ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS`` Django setting\n\n* Responses with ``Cache-Control: private``, ``no-cache``, or ``no-store``\n  directives are never cached.\n\n* Cached pages are keyed by request URL and vary by headers listed in the\n  response's ``Vary`` header (e.g., ``Vary: Accept-Language, Cookie``).\n\n* Responses that set user-specific cookies (detected via ``Vary: Cookie`` header)\n  on cache-less requests are not cached for security.\n\n* HEAD requests are served from GET cache entries when available. If no GET\n  cache entry exists, a separate HEAD cache entry may be used.\n\n* When a cache hit occurs, a shallow copy of the cached response is returned,\n  with updated ``Age`` header reflecting response age.\n\n* Response headers are automatically patched with ``ETag``, ``Last-Modified``,\n  ``Expires``, and ``Cache-Control`` headers.\n\nSettings\n========\n\n* ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS``: Default cache timeout in seconds. Default: 600.\n* ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX``: Prefix for all cache keys. Default: ''.\n* ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS``: Cache alias to use. Default: ``'default'``.\n\nSee the Django caching framework documentation for more information on cache\nconfiguration and the cache decorator.\n\"\"\"\n\nimport time\n\nfrom django.conf import settings\nfrom django.core.cache import DEFAULT_CACHE_ALIAS, caches\nfrom django.utils.cache import (\n    get_cache_key,\n    get_max_age,\n    has_vary_header,\n    learn_cache_key,\n    patch_response_headers,\n)\nfrom django.utils.deprecation import MiddlewareMixin\nfrom django.utils.http import parse_http_date_safe\n\n\nclass UpdateCacheMiddleware(MiddlewareMixin):\n    \"\"\"\n    Middleware that updates the cache with the response from the view.\n\n    This is the response-phase part of the two-part cache middleware system.\n    It caches the response if it is cacheable according to Django's caching rules.\n\n    When used with ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware``, ``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` should\n    be listed first in the ``MIDDLEWARE`` setting so that it runs last during the\n    response phase (middleware processes responses bottom-up).\n\n    Attributes:\n        cache_timeout (int): Default cache timeout in seconds, from\n            ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS`` setting.\n        key_prefix (str): Prefix for all cache keys, from\n            ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX`` setting.\n        cache_alias (str): Cache backend alias to use, from\n            ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS`` setting.\n        page_timeout (int, optional): Per-view cache timeout. Defaults to None.\n\n    Example:\n        Configuration in settings.py::\n\n            MIDDLEWARE = [\n                'django.middleware.cache.UpdateCacheMiddleware',\n                # ... other middleware ...\n                'django.middleware.cache.FetchFromCacheMiddleware',\n            ]\n\n            CACHES = {\n                'default': {\n                    'BACKEND': 'django.core.cache.backends.redis.RedisCache',\n                    'LOCATION': 'redis://127.0.0.1:6379/1',\n                }\n            }\n\n            CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS = 600\n            CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX = 'myapp'\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(self, get_response):\n        super().__init__(get_response)\n        self.cache_timeout = settings.CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS\n        self.page_timeout = None\n        self.key_prefix = settings.CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX\n        self.cache_alias = settings.CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS\n\n    @property\n    def cache(self):\n        return caches[self.cache_alias]\n\n    def _should_update_cache(self, request, response):\n        return hasattr(request, \"_cache_update_cache\") and request._cache_update_cache\n\n    def process_response(self, request, response):\n        \"\"\"\n        Cache the response if it is cacheable.\n\n        Responses are cached if:\n        - The request has ``_cache_update_cache`` attribute set to True\n        - The response status code is 200 or 304\n        - The response is not a streaming response\n        - The response does not set user-specific cookies on cache-less requests\n        - The Cache-Control header does not contain private/no-cache/no-store\n        - The cache timeout is non-zero\n\n        Cache timeout is determined from (in order of precedence):\n        1. ``self.page_timeout`` (instance attribute, may be set per-request)\n        2. ``max-age`` directive in the response's ``Cache-Control`` header\n        3. ``self.cache_timeout`` (from CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS setting)\n\n        If the response has a render method (e.g., TemplateResponse), caching is\n        deferred until after render using a post-render callback.\n\n        The Cache-Control and Expires headers are automatically patched on the\n        response to indicate cache validity. For GET requests with status 200,\n        the response is stored in the cache under a key derived from the request\n        URL and the headers listed in the Vary response header.\n\n        Args:\n            request (HttpRequest): The request object. Should have\n                ``_cache_update_cache`` attribute set by FetchFromCacheMiddleware.\n            response (HttpResponse): The response object to potentially cache.\n\n        Returns:\n            HttpResponse: The same response object, possibly with updated\n            Cache-Control, ETag, Last-Modified, and Expires headers.\n        \"\"\"\n        if not self._should_update_cache(request, response):\n            # We don't need to update the cache, just return.\n            return response\n\n        if response.streaming or response.status_code not in (200, 304):\n            return response\n\n        # Don't cache responses that set a user-specific (and maybe security\n        # sensitive) cookie in response to a cookie-less request.\n        if (\n            not request.COOKIES\n            and response.cookies\n            and has_vary_header(response, \"Cookie\")\n        ):\n            return response\n\n        # Don't cache responses when the Cache-Control header is set to\n        # private, no-cache, or no-store.\n        cache_control = response.get(\"Cache-Control\", ())\n        if any(\n            directive in cache_control\n            for directive in (\n                \"private\",\n                \"no-cache\",\n                \"no-store\",\n            )\n        ):\n            return response\n\n        # Page timeout takes precedence over the \"max-age\" and the default\n        # cache timeout.\n        timeout = self.page_timeout\n        if timeout is None:\n            # The timeout from the \"max-age\" section of the \"Cache-Control\"\n            # header takes precedence over the default cache timeout.\n            timeout = get_max_age(response)\n            if timeout is None:\n                timeout = self.cache_timeout\n            elif timeout == 0:\n                # max-age was set to 0, don't cache.\n                return response\n        patch_response_headers(response, timeout)\n        if timeout and response.status_code == 200:\n            cache_key = learn_cache_key(\n                request, response, timeout, self.key_prefix, cache=self.cache\n            )\n            if hasattr(response, \"render\") and callable(response.render):\n                response.add_post_render_callback(\n                    lambda r: self.cache.set(cache_key, r, timeout)\n                )\n            else:\n                self.cache.set(cache_key, response, timeout)\n        return response\n\n\nclass FetchFromCacheMiddleware(MiddlewareMixin):\n    \"\"\"\n    Middleware that fetches responses from the cache.\n\n    This is the request-phase part of the two-part cache middleware system.\n    It checks whether a cached response exists for the incoming request and\n    returns it if available, short-circuiting view execution.\n\n    When used with ``UpdateCacheMiddleware``, ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware``\n    should be listed last in the ``MIDDLEWARE`` setting so that it runs last\n    during the request phase (middleware processes requests top-down).\n\n    Attributes:\n        key_prefix (str): Prefix for all cache keys, from\n            ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX`` setting.\n        cache_alias (str): Cache backend alias to use, from\n            ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS`` setting.\n\n    Example:\n        Configuration in settings.py::\n\n            MIDDLEWARE = [\n                'django.middleware.cache.UpdateCacheMiddleware',\n                # ... other middleware ...\n                'django.middleware.cache.FetchFromCacheMiddleware',\n            ]\n\n    Note:\n        This middleware sets the ``_cache_update_cache`` attribute on the\n        request object to indicate whether UpdateCacheMiddleware should cache\n        the response. Set to False if a cached response is served or the request\n        method is not GET/HEAD. Set to True if cache lookup fails.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(self, get_response):\n        super().__init__(get_response)\n        self.key_prefix = settings.CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX\n        self.cache_alias = settings.CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS\n\n    @property\n    def cache(self):\n        return caches[self.cache_alias]\n\n    def process_request(self, request):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return a cached response if one is available for this request.\n\n        Only GET and HEAD requests are checked against the cache. Other request\n        methods are passed through to the view without caching.\n\n        The cache key is derived from the request URL and any headers specified\n        in a Vary header on the cached response. If a cached response is found,\n        it is returned as a shallow copy with the Age header set to indicate\n        how old the cached response is.\n\n        For HEAD requests, the middleware first attempts to find a cached GET\n        response. If none exists, it looks for a cached HEAD response.\n\n        This middleware sets the ``_cache_update_cache`` request attribute to\n        control whether the response should be cached by UpdateCacheMiddleware:\n        - False: A cached response was served (or request method is not GET/HEAD)\n        - True: Cache lookup failed, response should be cached if cacheable\n\n        Args:\n            request (HttpRequest): The incoming HTTP request.\n\n        Returns:\n            HttpResponse or None: A cached response if available, None otherwise.\n                Sets ``_cache_update_cache`` attribute on request to indicate\n                whether the response should be cached.\n\n        Side Effects:\n            - Sets ``request._cache_update_cache`` to True or False\n            - May set ``Age`` header on returned response to indicate cache age\n        \"\"\"\n        if request.method not in (\"GET\", \"HEAD\"):\n            request._cache_update_cache = False\n            return None  # Don't bother checking the cache.\n\n        # try and get the cached GET response\n        cache_key = get_cache_key(request, self.key_prefix, \"GET\", cache=self.cache)\n        if cache_key is None:\n            request._cache_update_cache = True\n            return None  # No cache information available, need to rebuild.\n        response = self.cache.get(cache_key)\n        # if it wasn't found and we are looking for a HEAD, try looking just\n        # for that\n        if response is None and request.method == \"HEAD\":\n            cache_key = get_cache_key(\n                request, self.key_prefix, \"HEAD\", cache=self.cache\n            )\n            response = self.cache.get(cache_key)\n\n        if response is None:\n            request._cache_update_cache = True\n            return None  # No cache information available, need to rebuild.\n\n        # Derive the age estimation of the cached response.\n        if (max_age_seconds := get_max_age(response)) is not None and (\n            expires_timestamp := parse_http_date_safe(response[\"Expires\"])\n        ) is not None:\n            now_timestamp = int(time.time())\n            remaining_seconds = expires_timestamp - now_timestamp\n            # Use Age: 0 if local clock got turned back.\n            response[\"Age\"] = max(0, max_age_seconds - remaining_seconds)\n\n        # hit, return cached response\n        request._cache_update_cache = False\n        return response\n\n\nclass CacheMiddleware(UpdateCacheMiddleware, FetchFromCacheMiddleware):\n    \"\"\"\n    Unified cache middleware combining request and response caching.\n\n    This middleware combines the functionality of ``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` and\n    ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware`` in a single class, suitable for simple sites\n    that don't require middleware to influence the cache key.\n\n    For more complex caching requirements (e.g., when other middleware like\n    ``LocaleMiddleware`` needs to affect the cache key), use the two-part\n    middleware (``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` and ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware``)\n    instead.\n\n    This class is also used as the hook point for the cache decorator, which\n    is generated using the decorator-from-middleware utility.\n\n    Args:\n        get_response (callable): The next middleware or view in the chain.\n        cache_timeout (int, optional): Cache timeout in seconds. If not provided,\n            defaults to ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS`` setting. If explicitly\n            None, falls back to the setting. Default: None.\n        page_timeout (int, optional): Per-view cache timeout in seconds,\n            takes precedence over Cache-Control max-age and cache_timeout.\n            Default: None.\n        **kwargs: Additional keyword arguments:\n            - key_prefix (str, optional): Prefix for all cache keys. If not\n              provided, defaults to ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX`` setting.\n              Pass empty string '' for no prefix.\n            - cache_alias (str, optional): Cache backend alias. If not provided,\n              defaults to ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS`` setting. Pass\n              ``DEFAULT_CACHE_ALIAS`` or a custom alias name.\n\n    Attributes:\n        cache_timeout (int): Cache timeout in seconds.\n        page_timeout (int, optional): Per-view cache timeout.\n        key_prefix (str): Prefix for cache keys.\n        cache_alias (str): Cache backend alias.\n\n    Example:\n        Simple configuration in settings.py::\n\n            MIDDLEWARE = [\n                'django.middleware.cache.CacheMiddleware',\n                # ... other middleware ...\n            ]\n\n            CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS = 600\n            CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX = 'myapp'\n            CACHES = {\n                'default': {\n                    'BACKEND': 'django.core.cache.backends.locmem.LocMemCache',\n                }\n            }\n\n        Or with custom parameters::\n\n            MIDDLEWARE = [\n                'django.middleware.cache.CacheMiddleware',\n            ]\n\n        With decorator usage::\n\n            from django.views.decorators.cache import cache_page\n\n            @cache_page(60 * 5)  # 5 minutes\n            def my_view(request):\n                return HttpResponse('Cached response')\n\n    Note:\n        When ``cache_timeout`` is provided as None (explicitly), the middleware\n        uses the ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS`` setting. When not provided at all\n        to __init__, the middleware uses its inherited default value.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(self, get_response, cache_timeout=None, page_timeout=None, **kwargs):\n        super().__init__(get_response)\n        # We need to differentiate between \"provided, but using default value\",\n        # and \"not provided\". If the value is provided using a default, then\n        # we fall back to system defaults. If it is not provided at all,\n        # we need to use middleware defaults.\n\n        try:\n            key_prefix = kwargs[\"key_prefix\"]\n            if key_prefix is None:\n                key_prefix = \"\"\n            self.key_prefix = key_prefix\n        except KeyError:\n            pass\n        try:\n            cache_alias = kwargs[\"cache_alias\"]\n            if cache_alias is None:\n                cache_alias = DEFAULT_CACHE_ALIAS\n            self.cache_alias = cache_alias\n        except KeyError:\n            pass\n\n        if cache_timeout is not None:\n            self.cache_timeout = cache_timeout\n        self.page_timeout = page_timeout\nDOCSTRING_EOF\n","description":"Prepare updated cache.py file with enhanced docstrings"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":189,"cache_read_input_tokens":27446,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":189},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"3f582ab0-8ae5-4ba1-8720-a835b0048ad0","uuid":"0ae79e74-8e73-420a-b975-fd1e7e6e776d"}

This approach allows other middleware to influence the\n    cache key (e.g., ``LocaleMiddleware`` for locale-aware caching).\n\n    .. code-block:: python\n\n        MIDDLEWARE = [\n            'django.middleware.cache.UpdateCacheMiddleware',\n            # ... other middleware ...\n            'django.middleware.cache.FetchFromCacheMiddleware'\n        ]\n\n    Important: ``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` must be listed first (runs last during\n    response phase), and ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware`` must be listed last (runs\n    last during request phase).\n\n**Single-Class Middleware**\n    For simple sites, use ``CacheMiddleware`` instead:\n\n    .. code-block:: python\n\n        MIDDLEWARE = [\n            'django.middleware.cache.CacheMiddleware',\n            # ... other middleware ...\n        ]\n\nCaching Behavior\n================\n\n* Only GET and HEAD requests with HTTP status code 200 are cached.\n\n* Cache timeout is determined by (in order of precedence):\n    1. ``page_timeout`` parameter (if using CacheMiddleware)\n    2. ``max-age`` directive in the response's ``Cache-Control`` header\n    3. ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS`` Django setting\n\n* Responses with ``Cache-Control: private``, ``no-cache``, or ``no-store``\n  directives are never cached.\n\n* Cached pages are keyed by request URL and vary by headers listed in the\n  response's ``Vary`` header (e.g., ``Vary: Accept-Language, Cookie``).\n\n* Responses that set user-specific cookies (detected via ``Vary: Cookie`` header)\n  on cache-less requests are not cached for security.\n\n* HEAD requests are served from GET cache entries when available. If no GET\n  cache entry exists, a separate HEAD cache entry may be used.\n\n* When a cache hit occurs, a shallow copy of the cached response is returned,\n  with updated ``Age`` header reflecting response age.\n\n* Response headers are automatically patched with ``ETag``, ``Last-Modified``,\n  ``Expires``, and ``Cache-Control`` headers.\n\nSettings\n========\n\n* ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS``: Default cache timeout in seconds. Default: 600.\n* ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX``: Prefix for all cache keys. Default: ''.\n* ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS``: Cache alias to use. Default: ``'default'``.\n\nSee the Django caching framework documentation for more information on cache\nconfiguration and the cache decorator.\n\"\"\"\n\nimport time\n\nfrom django.conf import settings\nfrom django.core.cache import DEFAULT_CACHE_ALIAS, caches\nfrom django.utils.cache import (\n    get_cache_key,\n    get_max_age,\n    has_vary_header,\n    learn_cache_key,\n    patch_response_headers,\n)\nfrom django.utils.deprecation import MiddlewareMixin\nfrom django.utils.http import parse_http_date_safe\n\n\nclass UpdateCacheMiddleware(MiddlewareMixin):\n    \"\"\"\n    Middleware that updates the cache with the response from the view.\n\n    This is the response-phase part of the two-part cache middleware system.\n    It caches the response if it is cacheable according to Django's caching rules.\n\n    When used with ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware``, ``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` should\n    be listed first in the ``MIDDLEWARE`` setting so that it runs last during the\n    response phase (middleware processes responses bottom-up).\n\n    Attributes:\n        cache_timeout (int): Default cache timeout in seconds, from\n            ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS`` setting.\n        key_prefix (str): Prefix for all cache keys, from\n            ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX`` setting.\n        cache_alias (str): Cache backend alias to use, from\n            ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS`` setting.\n        page_timeout (int, optional): Per-view cache timeout. Defaults to None.\n\n    Example:\n        Configuration in settings.py::\n\n            MIDDLEWARE = [\n                'django.middleware.cache.UpdateCacheMiddleware',\n                # ... other middleware ...\n                'django.middleware.cache.FetchFromCacheMiddleware',\n            ]\n\n            CACHES = {\n                'default': {\n                    'BACKEND': 'django.core.cache.backends.redis.RedisCache',\n                    'LOCATION': 'redis://127.0.0.1:6379/1',\n                }\n            }\n\n            CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS = 600\n            CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX = 'myapp'\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(self, get_response):\n        super().__init__(get_response)\n        self.cache_timeout = settings.CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS\n        self.page_timeout = None\n        self.key_prefix = settings.CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX\n        self.cache_alias = settings.CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS\n\n    @property\n    def cache(self):\n        return caches[self.cache_alias]\n\n    def _should_update_cache(self, request, response):\n        return hasattr(request, \"_cache_update_cache\") and request._cache_update_cache\n\n    def process_response(self, request, response):\n        \"\"\"\n        Cache the response if it is cacheable.\n\n        Responses are cached if:\n        - The request has ``_cache_update_cache`` attribute set to True\n        - The response status code is 200 or 304\n        - The response is not a streaming response\n        - The response does not set user-specific cookies on cache-less requests\n        - The Cache-Control header does not contain private/no-cache/no-store\n        - The cache timeout is non-zero\n\n        Cache timeout is determined from (in order of precedence):\n        1. ``self.page_timeout`` (instance attribute, may be set per-request)\n        2. ``max-age`` directive in the response's ``Cache-Control`` header\n        3. ``self.cache_timeout`` (from CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS setting)\n\n        If the response has a render method (e.g., TemplateResponse), caching is\n        deferred until after render using a post-render callback.\n\n        The Cache-Control and Expires headers are automatically patched on the\n        response to indicate cache validity. For GET requests with status 200,\n        the response is stored in the cache under a key derived from the request\n        URL and the headers listed in the Vary response header.\n\n        Args:\n            request (HttpRequest): The request object. Should have\n                ``_cache_update_cache`` attribute set by FetchFromCacheMiddleware.\n            response (HttpResponse): The response object to potentially cache.\n\n        Returns:\n            HttpResponse: The same response object, possibly with updated\n            Cache-Control, ETag, Last-Modified, and Expires headers.\n        \"\"\"\n        if not self._should_update_cache(request, response):\n            # We don't need to update the cache, just return.\n            return response\n\n        if response.streaming or response.status_code not in (200, 304):\n            return response\n\n        # Don't cache responses that set a user-specific (and maybe security\n        # sensitive) cookie in response to a cookie-less request.\n        if (\n            not request.COOKIES\n            and response.cookies\n            and has_vary_header(response, \"Cookie\")\n        ):\n            return response\n\n        # Don't cache responses when the Cache-Control header is set to\n        # private, no-cache, or no-store.\n        cache_control = response.get(\"Cache-Control\", ())\n        if any(\n            directive in cache_control\n            for directive in (\n                \"private\",\n                \"no-cache\",\n                \"no-store\",\n            )\n        ):\n            return response\n\n        # Page timeout takes precedence over the \"max-age\" and the default\n        # cache timeout.\n        timeout = self.page_timeout\n        if timeout is None:\n            # The timeout from the \"max-age\" section of the \"Cache-Control\"\n            # header takes precedence over the default cache timeout.\n            timeout = get_max_age(response)\n            if timeout is None:\n                timeout = self.cache_timeout\n            elif timeout == 0:\n                # max-age was set to 0, don't cache.\n                return response\n        patch_response_headers(response, timeout)\n        if timeout and response.status_code == 200:\n            cache_key = learn_cache_key(\n                request, response, timeout, self.key_prefix, cache=self.cache\n            )\n            if hasattr(response, \"render\") and callable(response.render):\n                response.add_post_render_callback(\n                    lambda r: self.cache.set(cache_key, r, timeout)\n                )\n            else:\n                self.cache.set(cache_key, response, timeout)\n        return response\n\n\nclass FetchFromCacheMiddleware(MiddlewareMixin):\n    \"\"\"\n    Middleware that fetches responses from the cache.\n\n    This is the request-phase part of the two-part cache middleware system.\n    It checks whether a cached response exists for the incoming request and\n    returns it if available, short-circuiting view execution.\n\n    When used with ``UpdateCacheMiddleware``, ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware``\n    should be listed last in the ``MIDDLEWARE`` setting so that it runs last\n    during the request phase (middleware processes requests top-down).\n\n    Attributes:\n        key_prefix (str): Prefix for all cache keys, from\n            ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX`` setting.\n        cache_alias (str): Cache backend alias to use, from\n            ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS`` setting.\n\n    Example:\n        Configuration in settings.py::\n\n            MIDDLEWARE = [\n                'django.middleware.cache.UpdateCacheMiddleware',\n                # ... other middleware ...\n                'django.middleware.cache.FetchFromCacheMiddleware',\n            ]\n\n    Note:\n        This middleware sets the ``_cache_update_cache`` attribute on the\n        request object to indicate whether UpdateCacheMiddleware should cache\n        the response. Set to False if a cached response is served or the request\n        method is not GET/HEAD. Set to True if cache lookup fails.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(self, get_response):\n        super().__init__(get_response)\n        self.key_prefix = settings.CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX\n        self.cache_alias = settings.CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS\n\n    @property\n    def cache(self):\n        return caches[self.cache_alias]\n\n    def process_request(self, request):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return a cached response if one is available for this request.\n\n        Only GET and HEAD requests are checked against the cache. Other request\n        methods are passed through to the view without caching.\n\n        The cache key is derived from the request URL and any headers specified\n        in a Vary header on the cached response. If a cached response is found,\n        it is returned as a shallow copy with the Age header set to indicate\n        how old the cached response is.\n\n        For HEAD requests, the middleware first attempts to find a cached GET\n        response. If none exists, it looks for a cached HEAD response.\n\n        This middleware sets the ``_cache_update_cache`` request attribute to\n        control whether the response should be cached by UpdateCacheMiddleware:\n        - False: A cached response was served (or request method is not GET/HEAD)\n        - True: Cache lookup failed, response should be cached if cacheable\n\n        Args:\n            request (HttpRequest): The incoming HTTP request.\n\n        Returns:\n            HttpResponse or None: A cached response if available, None otherwise.\n                Sets ``_cache_update_cache`` attribute on request to indicate\n                whether the response should be cached.\n\n        Side Effects:\n            - Sets ``request._cache_update_cache`` to True or False\n            - May set ``Age`` header on returned response to indicate cache age\n        \"\"\"\n        if request.method not in (\"GET\", \"HEAD\"):\n            request._cache_update_cache = False\n            return None  # Don't bother checking the cache.\n\n        # try and get the cached GET response\n        cache_key = get_cache_key(request, self.key_prefix, \"GET\", cache=self.cache)\n        if cache_key is None:\n            request._cache_update_cache = True\n            return None  # No cache information available, need to rebuild.\n        response = self.cache.get(cache_key)\n        # if it wasn't found and we are looking for a HEAD, try looking just\n        # for that\n        if response is None and request.method == \"HEAD\":\n            cache_key = get_cache_key(\n                request, self.key_prefix, \"HEAD\", cache=self.cache\n            )\n            response = self.cache.get(cache_key)\n\n        if response is None:\n            request._cache_update_cache = True\n            return None  # No cache information available, need to rebuild.\n\n        # Derive the age estimation of the cached response.\n        if (max_age_seconds := get_max_age(response)) is not None and (\n            expires_timestamp := parse_http_date_safe(response[\"Expires\"])\n        ) is not None:\n            now_timestamp = int(time.time())\n            remaining_seconds = expires_timestamp - now_timestamp\n            # Use Age: 0 if local clock got turned back.\n            response[\"Age\"] = max(0, max_age_seconds - remaining_seconds)\n\n        # hit, return cached response\n        request._cache_update_cache = False\n        return response\n\n\nclass CacheMiddleware(UpdateCacheMiddleware, FetchFromCacheMiddleware):\n    \"\"\"\n    Unified cache middleware combining request and response caching.\n\n    This middleware combines the functionality of ``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` and\n    ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware`` in a single class, suitable for simple sites\n    that don't require middleware to influence the cache key.\n\n    For more complex caching requirements (e.g., when other middleware like\n    ``LocaleMiddleware`` needs to affect the cache key), use the two-part\n    middleware (``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` and ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware``)\n    instead.\n\n    This class is also used as the hook point for the cache decorator, which\n    is generated using the decorator-from-middleware utility.\n\n    Args:\n        get_response (callable): The next middleware or view in the chain.\n        cache_timeout (int, optional): Cache timeout in seconds. If not provided,\n            defaults to ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS`` setting. If explicitly\n            None, falls back to the setting. Default: None.\n        page_timeout (int, optional): Per-view cache timeout in seconds,\n            takes precedence over Cache-Control max-age and cache_timeout.\n            Default: None.\n        **kwargs: Additional keyword arguments:\n            - key_prefix (str, optional): Prefix for all cache keys. If not\n              provided, defaults to ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX`` setting.\n              Pass empty string '' for no prefix.\n            - cache_alias (str, optional): Cache backend alias. If not provided,\n              defaults to ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS`` setting. Pass\n              ``DEFAULT_CACHE_ALIAS`` or a custom alias name.\n\n    Attributes:\n        cache_timeout (int): Cache timeout in seconds.\n        page_timeout (int, optional): Per-view cache timeout.\n        key_prefix (str): Prefix for cache keys.\n        cache_alias (str): Cache backend alias.\n\n    Example:\n        Simple configuration in settings.py::\n\n            MIDDLEWARE = [\n                'django.middleware.cache.CacheMiddleware',\n                # ... other middleware ...\n            ]\n\n            CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS = 600\n            CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX = 'myapp'\n            CACHES = {\n                'default': {\n                    'BACKEND': 'django.core.cache.backends.locmem.LocMemCache',\n                }\n            }\n\n        Or with custom parameters::\n\n            MIDDLEWARE = [\n                'django.middleware.cache.CacheMiddleware',\n            ]\n\n        With decorator usage::\n\n            from django.views.decorators.cache import cache_page\n\n            @cache_page(60 * 5)  # 5 minutes\n            def my_view(request):\n                return HttpResponse('Cached response')\n\n    Note:\n        When ``cache_timeout`` is provided as None (explicitly), the middleware\n        uses the ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS`` setting. When not provided at all\n        to __init__, the middleware uses its inherited default value.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(self, get_response, cache_timeout=None, page_timeout=None, **kwargs):\n        super().__init__(get_response)\n        # We need to differentiate between \"provided, but using default value\",\n        # and \"not provided\". If the value is provided using a default, then\n        # we fall back to system defaults. If it is not provided at all,\n        # we need to use middleware defaults.\n\n        try:\n            key_prefix = kwargs[\"key_prefix\"]\n            if key_prefix is None:\n                key_prefix = \"\"\n            self.key_prefix = key_prefix\n        except KeyError:\n            pass\n        try:\n            cache_alias = kwargs[\"cache_alias\"]\n            if cache_alias is None:\n                cache_alias = DEFAULT_CACHE_ALIAS\n            self.cache_alias = cache_alias\n        except KeyError:\n            pass\n\n        if cache_timeout is not None:\n            self.cache_timeout = cache_timeout\n        self.page_timeout = page_timeout\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":10,"cache_creation_input_tokens":266,"cache_read_input_tokens":34397,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":266},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"3f582ab0-8ae5-4ba1-8720-a835b0048ad0","uuid":"3a8fc90b-1847-47a1-a347-083aa54b4e12"}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_017dCyzzcWgChqQK86D2jteA","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01SRkhpCmY8yPCeUdXLz4oaE","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Django Cache Middleware Documentation\n\n## Overview\n\nThis document provides comprehensive Python docstrings generated for Django's cache middleware module (`django/middleware/cache.py`). The module implements full-page HTTP caching functionality.\n\n## File: `django/middleware/cache.py`\n\n### Module-Level Docstring\n\n```python\n\"\"\"\nFull-page cache middleware for Django.\n\nThis module provides cache middleware that caches entire HTTP responses based on\nthe request URL and method. When enabled, each Django-powered page will be\ncached and served from the cache on subsequent requests.\n\nConfiguration\n=============\n\nThere are two ways to enable caching:\n\n**Two-Part Middleware (Recommended)**\n    Use ``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` and ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware`` in your\n    middleware stack. This approach allows other middleware to influence the\n    cache key (e.g., ``LocaleMiddleware`` for locale-aware caching).\n\n    .. code-block:: python\n\n        MIDDLEWARE = [\n            'django.middleware.cache.UpdateCacheMiddleware',\n            # ... other middleware ...\n            'django.middleware.cache.FetchFromCacheMiddleware'\n        ]\n\n    Important: ``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` must be listed first (runs last during\n    response phase), and ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware`` must be listed last (runs\n    last during request phase).\n\n**Single-Class Middleware**\n    For simple sites, use ``CacheMiddleware`` instead:\n\n    .. code-block:: python\n\n        MIDDLEWARE = [\n            'django.middleware.cache.CacheMiddleware',\n            # ... other middleware ...\n        ]\n\nCaching Behavior\n================\n\n* Only GET and HEAD requests with HTTP status code 200 are cached.\n\n* Cache timeout is determined by (in order of precedence):\n    1. ``page_timeout`` parameter (if using CacheMiddleware)\n    2. ``max-age`` directive in the response's ``Cache-Control`` header\n    3. ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS`` Django setting\n\n* Responses with ``Cache-Control: private``, ``no-cache``, or ``no-store``\n  directives are never cached.\n\n* Cached pages are keyed by request URL and vary by headers listed in the\n  response's ``Vary`` header (e.g., ``Vary: Accept-Language, Cookie``).\n\n* Responses that set user-specific cookies (detected via ``Vary: Cookie`` header)\n  on cache-less requests are not cached for security.\n\n* HEAD requests are served from GET cache entries when available. If no GET\n  cache entry exists, a separate HEAD cache entry may be used.\n\n* When a cache hit occurs, a shallow copy of the cached response is returned,\n  with updated ``Age`` header reflecting response age.\n\n* Response headers are automatically patched with ``ETag``, ``Last-Modified``,\n  ``Expires``, and ``Cache-Control`` headers.\n\nSettings\n========\n\n* ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS``: Default cache timeout in seconds. Default: 600.\n* ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX``: Prefix for all cache keys. Default: ''.\n* ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS``: Cache alias to use. Default: ``'default'``.\n\nSee the Django caching framework documentation for more information on cache\nconfiguration and the cache decorator.\n\"\"\"\n```\n\n---\n\n## Documented Classes and Methods\n\n### 1. `UpdateCacheMiddleware`\n\n**Type:** Class (Response-phase middleware)\n\n**Purpose:** Updates the cache with response from the view if the response is cacheable.\n\n**Docstring:**\n\n```python\nclass UpdateCacheMiddleware(MiddlewareMixin):\n    \"\"\"\n    Middleware that updates the cache with the response from the view.\n\n    This is the response-phase part of the two-part cache middleware system.\n    It caches the response if it is cacheable according to Django's caching rules.\n\n    When used with ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware``, ``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` should\n    be listed first in the ``MIDDLEWARE`` setting so that it runs last during the\n    response phase (middleware processes responses bottom-up).\n\n    Attributes:\n        cache_timeout (int): Default cache timeout in seconds, from\n            ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS`` setting.\n        key_prefix (str): Prefix for all cache keys, from\n            ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX`` setting.\n        cache_alias (str): Cache backend alias to use, from\n            ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS`` setting.\n        page_timeout (int, optional): Per-view cache timeout. Defaults to None.\n\n    Example:\n        Configuration in settings.py::\n\n            MIDDLEWARE = [\n                'django.middleware.cache.UpdateCacheMiddleware',\n                # ... other middleware ...\n                'django.middleware.cache.FetchFromCacheMiddleware',\n            ]\n\n            CACHES = {\n                'default': {\n                    'BACKEND': 'django.core.cache.backends.redis.RedisCache',\n                    'LOCATION': 'redis://127.0.0.1:6379/1',\n                }\n            }\n\n            CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS = 600\n            CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX = 'myapp'\n    \"\"\"\n```\n\n#### Method: `process_response`\n\n**Signature:** `process_response(self, request, response) -> HttpResponse`\n\n**Docstring:**\n\n```python\ndef process_response(self, request, response):\n    \"\"\"\n    Cache the response if it is cacheable.\n\n    Responses are cached if:\n    - The request has ``_cache_update_cache`` attribute set to True\n    - The response status code is 200 or 304\n    - The response is not a streaming response\n    - The response does not set user-specific cookies on cache-less requests\n    - The Cache-Control header does not contain private/no-cache/no-store\n    - The cache timeout is non-zero\n\n    Cache timeout is determined from (in order of precedence):\n    1. ``self.page_timeout`` (instance attribute, may be set per-request)\n    2. ``max-age`` directive in the response's ``Cache-Control`` header\n    3. ``self.cache_timeout`` (from CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS setting)\n\n    If the response has a render method (e.g., TemplateResponse), caching is\n    deferred until after render using a post-render callback.\n\n    The Cache-Control and Expires headers are automatically patched on the\n    response to indicate cache validity. For GET requests with status 200,\n    the response is stored in the cache under a key derived from the request\n    URL and the headers listed in the Vary response header.\n\n    Args:\n        request (HttpRequest): The request object. Should have\n            ``_cache_update_cache`` attribute set by FetchFromCacheMiddleware.\n        response (HttpResponse): The response object to potentially cache.\n\n    Returns:\n        HttpResponse: The same response object, possibly with updated\n        Cache-Control, ETag, Last-Modified, and Expires headers.\n    \"\"\"\n```\n\n**Key Behaviors:**\n- **Cache-Control Header Handling:** Respects `Cache-Control: private`, `no-cache`, `no-store` directives and skips caching for responses with these directives\n- **Vary Header Interaction:** Uses the `Vary` header to determine cache key variations (especially important for Content-Language, Cookie, Accept-Encoding)\n- **Status Codes:** Only caches 200 and 304 responses\n- **Cookie Security:** Does not cache responses that set cookies on requests without cookies and have `Vary: Cookie` header\n- **Header Patching:** Automatically sets ETag, Last-Modified, Expires, and Cache-Control headers using `patch_response_headers()`\n- **Deferred Rendering:** For responses with a `render()` method, caching is deferred using `add_post_render_callback()`\n\n---\n\n### 2. `FetchFromCacheMiddleware`\n\n**Type:** Class (Request-phase middleware)\n\n**Purpose:** Checks whether a page is cached and returns the cached version if available.\n\n**Docstring:**\n\n```python\nclass FetchFromCacheMiddleware(MiddlewareMixin):\n    \"\"\"\n    Middleware that fetches responses from the cache.\n\n    This is the request-phase part of the two-part cache middleware system.\n    It checks whether a cached response exists for the incoming request and\n    returns it if available, short-circuiting view execution.\n\n    When used with ``UpdateCacheMiddleware``, ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware``\n    should be listed last in the ``MIDDLEWARE`` setting so that it runs last\n    during the request phase (middleware processes requests top-down).\n\n    Attributes:\n        key_prefix (str): Prefix for all cache keys, from\n            ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX`` setting.\n        cache_alias (str): Cache backend alias to use, from\n            ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS`` setting.\n\n    Example:\n        Configuration in settings.py::\n\n            MIDDLEWARE = [\n                'django.middleware.cache.UpdateCacheMiddleware',\n                # ... other middleware ...\n                'django.middleware.cache.FetchFromCacheMiddleware',\n            ]\n\n    Note:\n        This middleware sets the ``_cache_update_cache`` attribute on the\n        request object to indicate whether UpdateCacheMiddleware should cache\n        the response. Set to False if a cached response is served or the request\n        method is not GET/HEAD. Set to True if cache lookup fails.\n    \"\"\"\n```\n\n#### Method: `process_request`\n\n**Signature:** `process_request(self, request) -> HttpResponse or None`\n\n**Docstring:**\n\n```python\ndef process_request(self, request):\n    \"\"\"\n    Return a cached response if one is available for this request.\n\n    Only GET and HEAD requests are checked against the cache. Other request\n    methods are passed through to the view without caching.\n\n    The cache key is derived from the request URL and any headers specified\n    in a Vary header on the cached response. If a cached response is found,\n    it is returned as a shallow copy with the Age header set to indicate\n    how old the cached response is.\n\n    For HEAD requests, the middleware first attempts to find a cached GET\n    response. If none exists, it looks for a cached HEAD response.\n\n    This middleware sets the ``_cache_update_cache`` request attribute to\n    control whether the response should be cached by UpdateCacheMiddleware:\n    - False: A cached response was served (or request method is not GET/HEAD)\n    - True: Cache lookup failed, response should be cached if cacheable\n\n    Args:\n        request (HttpRequest): The incoming HTTP request.\n\n    Returns:\n        HttpResponse or None: A cached response if available, None otherwise.\n            Sets ``_cache_update_cache`` attribute on request to indicate\n            whether the response should be cached.\n\n    Side Effects:\n        - Sets ``request._cache_update_cache`` to True or False\n        - May set ``Age`` header on returned response to indicate cache age\n    \"\"\"\n```\n\n**Key Behaviors:**\n- **Method Filtering:** Only GET and HEAD requests are checked; other methods return None with `_cache_update_cache = False`\n- **Cache Key Derivation:** Uses `get_cache_key()` to generate cache key from request URL and Vary headers\n- **HEAD Request Fallback:** Attempts to serve HEAD requests from cached GET entries; falls back to cached HEAD entries\n- **Age Header Calculation:** Sets the `Age` header on cached responses using the difference between `max-age` and remaining cache time\n- **Request Flag Setting:** Always sets `request._cache_update_cache` to guide UpdateCacheMiddleware's behavior\n- **Shallow Copy:** Returns a shallow copy of the cached response (not the original object)\n\n---\n\n### 3. `CacheMiddleware`\n\n**Type:** Class (Combined middleware, inherits from both UpdateCacheMiddleware and FetchFromCacheMiddleware)\n\n**Purpose:** Unified cache middleware for simple sites that don't need other middleware to influence the cache key.\n\n**Docstring:**\n\n```python\nclass CacheMiddleware(UpdateCacheMiddleware, FetchFromCacheMiddleware):\n    \"\"\"\n    Unified cache middleware combining request and response caching.\n\n    This middleware combines the functionality of ``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` and\n    ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware`` in a single class, suitable for simple sites\n    that don't require middleware to influence the cache key.\n\n    For more complex caching requirements (e.g., when other middleware like\n    ``LocaleMiddleware`` needs to affect the cache key), use the two-part\n    middleware (``UpdateCacheMiddleware`` and ``FetchFromCacheMiddleware``)\n    instead.\n\n    This class is also used as the hook point for the cache decorator, which\n    is generated using the decorator-from-middleware utility.\n\n    Args:\n        get_response (callable): The next middleware or view in the chain.\n        cache_timeout (int, optional): Cache timeout in seconds. If not provided,\n            defaults to ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS`` setting. If explicitly\n            None, falls back to the setting. Default: None.\n        page_timeout (int, optional): Per-view cache timeout in seconds,\n            takes precedence over Cache-Control max-age and cache_timeout.\n            Default: None.\n        **kwargs: Additional keyword arguments:\n            - key_prefix (str, optional): Prefix for all cache keys. If not\n              provided, defaults to ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX`` setting.\n              Pass empty string '' for no prefix.\n            - cache_alias (str, optional): Cache backend alias. If not provided,\n              defaults to ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_ALIAS`` setting. Pass\n              ``DEFAULT_CACHE_ALIAS`` or a custom alias name.\n\n    Attributes:\n        cache_timeout (int): Cache timeout in seconds.\n        page_timeout (int, optional): Per-view cache timeout.\n        key_prefix (str): Prefix for cache keys.\n        cache_alias (str): Cache backend alias.\n\n    Example:\n        Simple configuration in settings.py::\n\n            MIDDLEWARE = [\n                'django.middleware.cache.CacheMiddleware',\n                # ... other middleware ...\n            ]\n\n            CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS = 600\n            CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_KEY_PREFIX = 'myapp'\n            CACHES = {\n                'default': {\n                    'BACKEND': 'django.core.cache.backends.locmem.LocMemCache',\n                }\n            }\n\n        Or with custom parameters::\n\n            MIDDLEWARE = [\n                'django.middleware.cache.CacheMiddleware',\n            ]\n\n        With decorator usage::\n\n            from django.views.decorators.cache import cache_page\n\n            @cache_page(60 * 5)  # 5 minutes\n            def my_view(request):\n                return HttpResponse('Cached response')\n\n    Note:\n        When ``cache_timeout`` is provided as None (explicitly), the middleware\n        uses the ``CACHE_MIDDLEWARE_SECONDS`` setting. When not provided at all\n        to __init__, the middleware uses its inherited default value.\n    \"\"\"\n```\n\n**Key Behaviors:**\n- **Parameter Differentiation:** The `__init__` method carefully distinguishes between \"not provided\" vs. \"explicitly None\" to properly handle defaults\n- **Keyword Argument Handling:** `key_prefix` and `cache_alias` can be passed via kwargs; if None is passed,
